      <p><b>Indonesia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ʒ/: 's' in 'pleasure'">ʒ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Indonesia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/En-us-Indonesia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Indonesia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">IN</span>-də-<span style="font-size:90%">NEE</span>-zhə</i></a>), officially the <b>Republic of Indonesia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Republik Indonesia</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malay" title="Help:IPA/Malay">[reˈpublik ɪndoˈnesia]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Id-Indonesia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/Id-Indonesia.ogg" class="internal" title="Id-Indonesia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-efn0_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-efn0-13">[a]</a></sup> is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, between the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> oceans. It consists of more than <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Indonesia" title="List of islands of Indonesia">seventeen thousand islands</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>) and <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> (<a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Papua</a>). Indonesia is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">14th-largest country by land area</a>, at 1,904,569 square kilometres (735,358 <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">square miles</a>). With more than 270.2 million people,<sup id="cite_ref-2020census_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020census-9">[9]</a></sup> Indonesia is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">fourth-most populous country</a> as well as the most populous <a href="/wiki/Islam_by_country" title="Islam by country">Muslim-majority country</a>. <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_population" title="List of islands by population">most populous island</a>, is home to more than half of the country's population. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> is a <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">presidential</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">constitutional republic</a> with an elected <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Consultative_Assembly" title="People's Consultative Assembly">legislature</a>. It has <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">34 provinces</a>, of which five have <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">special status</a>. The country's capital, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">second-most populous urban area in the world</a>. The country shares <a href="/wiki/Template:Borders_of_Indonesia" title="Template:Borders of Indonesia">land borders</a> with <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">eastern part</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. Other neighbouring countries include <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a>. Despite its large population and densely populated regions, Indonesia has vast areas of wilderness that support one of the <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">world's highest levels of biodiversity</a>. </p>
      <p>The Indonesian archipelago has been a valuable region for trade since at least the 7th century when <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> traded with entities from <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>. Local rulers gradually absorbed foreign influences from the early centuries and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Indonesia" title="Buddhism in Indonesia">Buddhist</a> kingdoms flourished. <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> traders and <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> scholars brought <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Islam</a>, while Europeans introduced <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Indonesia" title="Christianity in Indonesia">Christianity</a> through <a href="/wiki/European_colonisation_of_Southeast_Asia" title="European colonisation of Southeast Asia">colonisation</a>. Although sometimes interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonialism_in_the_East_Indies" title="Portuguese colonialism in the East Indies">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_and_British_interregnum_in_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="French and British interregnum in the Dutch East Indies">French and British</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies#History" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch</a> were the foremost <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">colonial power</a> for much of their 350-year presence in the archipelago. The concept of "Indonesia" as a nation-state <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Awakening" title="Indonesian National Awakening">emerged</a> in the early 20th century<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> and the country <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_Indonesian_Independence" title="Proclamation of Indonesian Independence">proclaimed its independence</a> in 1945. However, it was not until 1949 that the Dutch recognised <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Indonesia" title="United States of Indonesia">Indonesia's sovereignty</a> following an <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">armed and diplomatic conflict</a> between the two. </p>
      <p>Indonesia consists of hundreds of distinct native <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">ethnic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">linguistic</a> groups, with the largest one being the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>. A shared identity has developed with the motto <i>"<a href="/wiki/Bhinneka_Tunggal_Ika" title="Bhinneka Tunggal Ika">Bhinneka Tunggal Ika</a>"</i> ("Unity in Diversity" <i>literally</i>, "many, yet one"), defined by a national language, ethnic diversity, religious pluralism within a Muslim-majority population, and a history of colonialism and rebellion against it. The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia" title="Economy of Indonesia">economy of Indonesia</a> is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">16th</a> largest by nominal GDP and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">7th</a> by GDP at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>. Indonesia is the only <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and is considered a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in global affairs. The country is a member of several multilateral organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>, and a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN), <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>. </p>
