        </div> 
        <div style="position:absolute; left:547.333328px; top:228px">
         <a href="/wiki/Maluku_(province)" title="Maluku (province)">Maluku</a>
        </div> 
        <div style="position:absolute; left:622px; top:173.333336px">
         <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West<br>Papua</a>
        </div> 
        <div style="position:absolute; left:710px; top:214.666672px">
         <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">Papua</a>
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Indonesia" title="Foreign relations of Indonesia">Foreign relations of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/220px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/330px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/440px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Indonesia,_Canberra" title="Embassy of Indonesia, Canberra">Embassy of Indonesia, Canberra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia maintains 132 diplomatic missions abroad, including 95 embassies.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> The country adheres to what it calls a "free and active" foreign policy, seeking a role in regional affairs in proportion to its size and location but avoiding involvement in conflicts among other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia was a significant battleground during the Cold War. Numerous attempts by the United States and the Soviet Union,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> and China to some degree,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> culminated in the 1965 coup attempt and subsequent upheaval that led to a reorientation of foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-Robinson2018_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson2018-138">[137]</a></sup> Quiet alignment with the Western world while maintaining a non-aligned stance has characterised Indonesia's foreign policy since then.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Today, it maintains close relations with its neighbours and is a founding member of the Association of Southeast Asian Nations (<a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>. In common with most of the Muslim world, Indonesia does not have diplomatic relations with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and has actively supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>. However, observers have pointed out that Indonesia has ties with Israel, albeit discreetly.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has been <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_and_the_United_Nations" title="Indonesia and the United Nations">a member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1950 and was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (NAM) and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Indonesia is a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Free_Trade_Area" title="ASEAN Free Trade Area">ASEAN Free Trade Area</a> agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Cairns_Group" title="Cairns Group">Cairns Group</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), and an occasional member of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation">Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation</a>, Indonesia withdrew from the UN due to the latter's election to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, although it returned 18 months later. It marked the first time in UN history that a member state had attempted a withdrawal.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> Indonesia has been a humanitarian and development aid recipient since 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> and recently, the country established its first overseas aid program in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian National Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Indonesia" title="Military history of Indonesia">Military history of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:139px;max-width:139px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tniadkostrad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tniadkostrad.jpg/137px-Tniadkostrad.jpg" decoding="async" width="137" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tniadkostrad.jpg/206px-Tniadkostrad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tniadkostrad.jpg/274px-Tniadkostrad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:149px;max-width:149px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg/147px-Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="147" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg/221px-Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg/294px-Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="581" data-file-height="359"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:140px;max-width:140px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG/138px-RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG" decoding="async" width="138" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG/207px-RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG/276px-RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:148px;max-width:148px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/146px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg" decoding="async" width="146" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/219px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/292px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="600"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Indonesian Armed Forces. Clockwise from top: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Army" title="Indonesian Army">Indonesian Army</a> during training session, <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-30" title="Sukhoi Su-30">Sukhoi Su-30</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anoa_(armoured_personnel_carrier)" title="Anoa (armoured personnel carrier)">Pindad Anoa</a>, and Indonesian naval vessel KRI Sultan Iskandar Muda 367.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia's Armed Forces (TNI) include the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Army" title="Indonesian Army">Army</a> (TNI–AD), <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Navy" title="Indonesian Navy">Navy</a> (TNI–AL, which includes <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Marine_Corps" title="Indonesian Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Air_Force" title="Indonesian Air Force">Air Force</a> (TNI–AU). The army has about 400,000 active-duty personnel. Defence spending in the national budget was 0.7% of GDP in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> with controversial involvement of military-owned commercial interests and foundations.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> The Armed Forces were formed during the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a> when it undertook guerrilla warfare along with informal militia. Since then, territorial lines have formed the basis of all TNI branches' structure, aimed at maintaining domestic stability and deterring foreign threats.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> The military has possessed a strong political influence since its founding, which <a href="/wiki/Dwifungsi" title="Dwifungsi">peaked during the New Order</a>. Political reforms in 1998 included the removal of the TNI's formal representation from the legislature. Nevertheless, its political influence remains, albeit at a reduced level.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since independence, the country has struggled to maintain unity against local insurgencies and separatist movements.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> Some, notably in <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_Aceh" title="Insurgency in Aceh">Aceh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua</a>, have led to an armed conflict, and subsequent allegations of human rights abuses and brutality from all sides.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003270–273,_477–480_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003270–273,_477–480-153">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> The former was resolved peacefully in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-AcehPeace_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AcehPeace-74">[73]</a></sup> while the latter continues, amid a significant, albeit imperfect, implementation of regional autonomy laws, and a reported decline in the levels of violence and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Indonesia#West_Papua_issues" title="Human rights in Indonesia">human rights abuses</a> since 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> Other engagements of the army include the campaign against the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_New_Guinea" title="Netherlands New Guinea">Netherlands New Guinea</a> to incorporate the territory into Indonesia, the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation"><i>Konfrontasi</i></a> to oppose the creation of Malaysia, the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965–66">mass killings</a> of PKI, and the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">invasion of East Timor</a>, which remains Indonesia's most massive military operation.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia" title="Economy of Indonesia">Economy of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Indonesia" title="Economic history of Indonesia">Economic history of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jakarta_Panorama.jpg/220px-Jakarta_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jakarta_Panorama.jpg/330px-Jakarta_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Jakarta_Panorama.jpg/440px-Jakarta_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2772" data-file-height="1355"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, the capital city and the country's commercial centre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> in which both the private sector and government play vital roles.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> As the only <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> member state in Southeast Asia,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> the country has the largest economy in the region and is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Newly industrialised country">newly industrialised country</a>. As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">16th largest economy by nominal GDP</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">7th in terms of GDP at PPP</a>, estimated to be US$1.100&nbsp;trillion and US$3.740&nbsp;trillion respectively. Per capita GDP in PPP is US$14,020, while nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">per capita GDP</a> is US$4,120. The debt ratio to GDP is 29.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> The services are the economy's largest sector and account for 43.4% of GDP (2018), followed by industry (39.7%) and agriculture (12.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> Since 2009, it has employed more people than other sectors, accounting for 47.7% of the total labour force, followed by agriculture (30.2%) and industry (21.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/220px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/330px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/440px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vast <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> plantation in Bogor, West Java. Indonesia is the world's largest producer of palm oil.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Over time, the structure of the economy has changed considerably.<sup id="cite_ref-RBA_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-164">[163]</a></sup> Historically, it has been weighted heavily towards agriculture, reflecting both its stage of economic development and government policies in the 1950s and 1960s to promote agricultural self-sufficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-RBA_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-164">[163]</a></sup> A gradual process of industrialisation and urbanisation began in the late 1960s and accelerated in the 1980s as falling oil prices saw the government focus on diversifying away from oil exports and towards manufactured exports.<sup id="cite_ref-RBA_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-164">[163]</a></sup> This development continued throughout the 1980s and into the next decade despite the <a href="/wiki/1990_oil_price_shock" title="1990 oil price shock">1990 oil price shock</a>, during which the GDP rose at an average rate of 7.1%. As a result, the official poverty rate fell from 60% to 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> Reduction of trade barriers from the mid-1980s made the economy more globally integrated. The growth ended with the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a> that had a severe impact on the economy, including a 13.1% real GDP contraction in 1998 and inflation reaching 78%. The economy reached its low point in mid-1999 with only 0.8% real GDP growth.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Relatively steady inflation<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> and an increase in GDP deflator and the Consumer Price Index<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> have contributed to strong economic growth in recent years. From 2007 to 2019, annual growth has accelerated to between 4% and 6% as a result of improvement in the banking sector and domestic consumption,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> helping Indonesia weather the 2008–2009 <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> and regain in 2011 the investment grade rating it had lost in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 9.41% of the population lived below the poverty line, and the official open unemployment rate was 5.28%.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> However, in late 2020, Indonesia fell into its first recession in 22 years due to the effects of the global <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has abundant natural resources like <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Indonesia" title="Agriculture in Indonesia">agriculture</a> produces <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cacao_bean" class="mw-redirect" title="Cacao bean">cacao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">medicinal plants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">rubber</a>. These commodities make up a large portion of the country's exports, with palm oil and coal briquettes as the leading export commodities. In addition to refined and crude petroleum as the main imports, telephones, vehicle parts and wheat cover the majority of additional imports. China, the United States, Japan, Singapore, India, Malaysia, South Korea and Thailand are Indonesia's principal export markets and import partners.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Indonesia" title="Transport in Indonesia">Transport in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:138px;max-width:138px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:98px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/136px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="136" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/204px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/272px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2196" data-file-height="1592"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:150px;max-width:150px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:98px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/148px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG" decoding="async" width="148" height="98" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/222px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/296px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1624"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:137px;max-width:137px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:101px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/135px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg" decoding="async" width="135" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/203px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/270px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:151px;max-width:151px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:101px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg/149px-Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="149" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg/224px-Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg/298px-Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_737-800_Spijkers-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="817"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Major transport modes in Indonesia. Clockwise from top: TransJakarta bus, Jabodetabek Commuter Line, Garuda Indonesia Boeing 737-800, Pelni ship.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia's transport system has been shaped over time by the economic resource base of an archipelago, and the distribution of its 250&nbsp;million people highly concentrated on <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> All transport modes play a role in the country's transport system and are generally complementary rather than competitive. In 2016, the transport sector generated about 5.2% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The road transport system is predominant, with a total length of 542,310 kilometres (336,980 miles) as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup> Jakarta has the <a href="/wiki/TransJakarta" title="TransJakarta">most extended bus rapid transit system in the world</a>, boasting some 251.2 kilometres (156.1 miles) in 13 corridors and ten cross-corridor routes.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rickshaw" title="Rickshaw">Rickshaws</a> such as <i>bajaj</i> and <i>becak</i> and <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">share taxis</a> such as <i>Angkot</i> and <i>Metromini</i> are a regular sight in the country. Most of the railways are in Java, used for both freight and passenger transport, such as local commuter rail services complementing the inter-city rail network in several cities. In the late 2010s, Jakarta and Palembang were the first cities in Indonesia to have <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> systems, with more planned for other cities in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> In 2015, the government announced a plan to build a <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Indonesia" title="High-speed rail in Indonesia">high-speed rail</a>, which would be a first in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia's largest airport, <a href="/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport" title="Soekarno–Hatta International Airport">Soekarno–Hatta International Airport</a> is among the busiest in the Southern Hemisphere, <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">serving 54&nbsp;million passengers in 2019</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ngurah_Rai_International_Airport" title="Ngurah Rai International Airport">Ngurah Rai International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juanda_International_Airport" title="Juanda International Airport">Juanda International Airport</a> are the country's second-and third-busiest airport respectively. <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a>, the country's flag carrier since 1949, is one of the world's leading airlines and a member of the global airline alliance <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tanjung_Priok" title="Port of Tanjung Priok">Port of Tanjung Priok</a> is the busiest and most advanced Indonesian port,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> handling more than 50% of Indonesia's trans-shipment cargo traffic. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Indonesia" title="Energy in Indonesia">Energy in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2017, Indonesia was the world's 9th largest energy producer with 4,200 <a href="/wiki/Watt-hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Watt-hour">terawatt-hours</a> (14.2&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/1000000000000000_(number)" class="mw-redirect" title="1000000000000000 (number)">quadrillion</a> <a href="/wiki/British_thermal_unit" title="British thermal unit">British thermal units</a>), and the 15th largest energy consumer, with 2,100 terawatt-hours (7.1&nbsp;quadrillion British thermal units).<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> The country has substantial energy resources, including 22&nbsp;billion barrels (3.5&nbsp;billion cubic metres) of conventional oil and gas reserves (of which about 4&nbsp;billion barrels are recoverable), 8&nbsp;billion barrels of oil-equivalent of coal-based methane (CBM) resources, and 28&nbsp;billion tonnes of recoverable coal.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> While reliance on domestic coal and imported oil has increased,<sup id="cite_ref-IRENA_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA-184">[183]</a></sup> Indonesia has seen progress in renewable energy with hydropower being the most abundant source. Furthermore, the country has the potential for geothermal, solar, wind, biomass and ocean energy.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup> Indonesia has set out to achieve 23% use of renewable energy by 2025 and 31% by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-IRENA_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRENA-184">[183]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Indonesia's total national installed power generation capacity stands at 55,528.51 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's largest dam, <a href="/wiki/Jatiluhur_Dam" title="Jatiluhur Dam">Jatiluhur</a>, has several purposes including the provision of hydroelectric power generation, water supply, flood control, irrigation and <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>. The earth-fill dam is 105&nbsp;m (344&nbsp;ft) high and withholds a reservoir of 3.0&nbsp;billion&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup> (2.4&nbsp;million&nbsp;acre⋅ft). It helps to supply water to Jakarta and to irrigate 240,000&nbsp;ha (590,000 acres) of rice fields<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> and has an installed capacity of 186.5 MW which feeds into the Java grid managed by the State Electricity Company (<i><a href="/wiki/Perusahaan_Listrik_Negara" title="Perusahaan Listrik Negara">Perusahaan Listrik Negara</a></i>, PLN). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Indonesia" title="Science and technology in Indonesia">Science and technology in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/220px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/330px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/440px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2020" data-file-height="2020"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Palapa" title="Palapa">Palapa</a> satellite launch in 1984
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia's expenditure on science and technology is relatively low, at less than 0.1% of GDP (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> Historical examples of scientific and technological developments include the paddy cultivation technique <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(agriculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrace (agriculture)"><i>terasering</i></a>, which is common in Southeast Asia, and the <a href="/wiki/Pinisi" title="Pinisi">pinisi</a> boats by the <a href="/wiki/Bugis" class="mw-redirect" title="Bugis">Bugis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Makassar_people" title="Makassar people">Makassar people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> In the 1980s, Indonesian engineer <a href="/wiki/Tjokorda_Raka_Sukawati" title="Tjokorda Raka Sukawati">Tjokorda Raka Sukawati</a> invented a road construction technique named <a href="/wiki/Sosrobahu" title="Sosrobahu">Sosrobahu</a> that allows the construction of long stretches of flyovers above existing main roads with minimum traffic disruption. It later became widely used in several countries.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> The country is also an active producer of passenger trains and freight wagons with its state-owned company, the <a href="/wiki/Industri_Kereta_Api" title="Industri Kereta Api">Indonesian Railway Industry</a> (INKA), and has exported trains abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has a long history in developing military and small commuter aircraft as the only country in Southeast Asia to build and produce aircraft. With its state-owned company, the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Aerospace" title="Indonesian Aerospace">Indonesian Aerospace</a> (<i>PT. Dirgantara Indonesia</i>), Indonesia has provided components for <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>. The company also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/EADS_CASA" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS CASA">EADS CASA</a> of Spain to develop the <a href="/wiki/CASA/IPTN_CN-235" title="CASA/IPTN CN-235">CN-235</a> that has seen use by several countries.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> Former President <a href="/wiki/B._J._Habibie" title="B. J. Habibie">B. J. Habibie</a> played a vital role in this achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> Indonesia has also joined the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> programme to manufacture the fifth-generation jet fighter <a href="/wiki/KAI_KF-X" title="KAI KF-X">KAI KF-X</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has a space programme and space agency, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Aeronautics_and_Space" title="National Institute of Aeronautics and Space">National Institute of Aeronautics and Space</a> (<i>Lembaga Penerbangan dan Antariksa Nasional</i>, LAPAN). In the 1970s, Indonesia became the first developing country to operate a satellite system called <a href="/wiki/Palapa" title="Palapa">Palapa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> a series of communication satellites owned by <a href="/wiki/Indosat_Ooredoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Indosat Ooredoo">Indosat Ooredoo</a>. The first satellite, PALAPA A1 was launched on 8 July 1976 from the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a> in Florida, United States.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Indonesia has launched 18 satellites for various purposes,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> and LAPAN has expressed a desire to put satellites in orbit with native launch vehicles by 2040.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Indonesia" title="Tourism in Indonesia">Tourism in Indonesia</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/250px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/375px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/500px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1108"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a>, the world's largest Buddhist temple, is the single most visited tourist attraction in Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Indonesia" title="Tourism in Indonesia">Tourism</a> contributed around US$19.7&nbsp;billion to GDP in 2019. In 2018, Indonesia received 15.8&nbsp;million visitors, a growth of 12.5% from last year, and received an average receipt of US$967.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> China, Singapore, Malaysia, Australia, and Japan are the top five sources of visitors to Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> Since 2011, <i>Wonderful Indonesia</i> has been the slogan of the country's international marketing campaign to promote tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Raja_Ampat_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/220px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/330px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/440px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Raja_Ampat_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Raja_Ampat_Islands" title="Raja Ampat Islands">Raja Ampat Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West Papua</a>, has the highest recorded level of diversity in marine life, according to <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nature and culture are prime attractions of Indonesian tourism. The former can boast a unique combination of a tropical climate, a vast archipelago, and a long stretch of beaches, and the latter complement those with a rich cultural heritage reflecting Indonesia's dynamic history and ethnic diversity. Indonesia has a well-preserved natural ecosystem with rain forests that stretch over about 57% of Indonesia's land (225&nbsp;million acres). Forests on Sumatra and Kalimantan are examples of popular destinations, such as the Orangutan wildlife reserve. Moreover, Indonesia has one of the world's longest coastlines, measuring 54,716 kilometres (33,999&nbsp;mi). The ancient <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prambanan" title="Prambanan">Prambanan</a> temples as well as <a href="/wiki/Toraja" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraja">Toraja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, with its traditional festivities, are some of the popular destinations for cultural tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-pariwisata_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pariwisata-205">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Indonesia" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Indonesia">nine UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Komodo_National_Park" title="Komodo National Park">Komodo National Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ombilin_Coal_Mine" title="Ombilin Coal Mine">Sawahlunto Coal Mine</a>; and a further 19 in a tentative list that includes <a href="/wiki/Bunaken_National_Park" title="Bunaken National Park">Bunaken National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raja_Ampat_Islands" title="Raja Ampat Islands">Raja Ampat Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> Other attractions include the specific points in Indonesian history, such as the colonial heritage of the Dutch East Indies in the <a href="/wiki/Old_town" title="Old town">old towns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kota_Tua_Jakarta" title="Kota Tua Jakarta">Jakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_architecture_in_Semarang" title="Dutch architecture in Semarang">Semarang</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_palaces_in_Indonesia" title="List of palaces in Indonesia">royal palaces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pagaruyung_Palace" title="Pagaruyung Palace">Pagaruyung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubud_Palace" title="Ubud Palace">Ubud</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kraton_Ngayogyakarta_Hadiningrat" title="Kraton Ngayogyakarta Hadiningrat">Yogyakarta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pariwisata_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pariwisata-205">[204]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Indonesia" title="Demographics of Indonesia">Demographics of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesians" title="Indonesians">Indonesians</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_cities_by_population" title="List of Indonesian cities by population">List of Indonesian cities by population</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Indonesia" title="List of metropolitan areas in Indonesia">List of metropolitan areas in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Indonesian_census" title="2020 Indonesian census">2020 census</a> recorded <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Indonesia" title="Demographics of Indonesia">Indonesia's population</a> as 270.2&nbsp;million, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">fourth largest in the world</a>, with a moderately high population growth rate at 1.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> is the world's most populous island,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> where 56% of the country's population lives.<sup id="cite_ref-2020census_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020census-9">[9]</a></sup> The population density is 141 people per km<sup>2</sup> (365 per sq mi), ranking 88th in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> although Java has a population density of 1,067 people per km<sup>2</sup> (2,435 per sq mi). In 1961, the first post-colonial census recorded a total of 97&nbsp;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> It is expected to grow to around 295&nbsp;million by 2030 and 321&nbsp;million by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> The country currently possesses a relatively young population, with a median age of 30.2 years (2017 estimate).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The spread of the population is uneven throughout the archipelago with a varying habitat and level of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_provinces_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of Indonesian provinces by Human Development Index">development</a>, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> of Jakarta to <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted tribes</a> in Papua.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> As of 2017, about 54.7% of the population lives in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> Jakarta is the country's <a href="/wiki/Primate_city" title="Primate city">primate city</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">second-most populous urban area in the world</a> with over 34&nbsp;million residents.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> About 8&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Indonesians" title="Overseas Indonesians">Indonesians live overseas</a>; most settled in Malaysia, the Netherlands, Saudi Arabia, the United Arab Emirates, Hong Kong, Singapore, the United States, and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> </p>
