      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups_and_languages">Ethnic groups and languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">Ethnic groups in Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Native_Indonesians" title="Native Indonesians">Native Indonesians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">Languages of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/330px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/495px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/660px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="215"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of ethnic groups in Indonesia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesia is an ethnically diverse country, with around 600 distinct native ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-BPS_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> Most Indonesians are descended from <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a> whose languages had origins in <a href="/wiki/Proto-Austronesian_language" title="Proto-Austronesian language">Proto-Austronesian</a>, which possibly originated in what is now <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Another major grouping is the <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesians</a>, who inhabit eastern Indonesia (the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor20035–7_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor20035–7-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003139,_181,_251,_435_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003139,_181,_251,_435-216">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> are the largest ethnic group, constituting 40.2% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-BPS_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> and are politically dominant.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> They are predominantly located in the central to eastern parts of Java and also sizable numbers in most provinces. The <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Batak people">Batak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madurese_people" title="Madurese people">Madurese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bugis_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bugis people">Buginese</a> are the next largest groups in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[b]</a></sup> A sense of Indonesian nationhood exists alongside strong regional identities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991256_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991256-220">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's official language is <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, a variant of <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> based on its <a href="/wiki/Prestige_(sociolinguistics)" title="Prestige (sociolinguistics)">prestige dialect</a>, which for centuries had been the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> of the archipelago. It was <a href="/wiki/Youth_Pledge" title="Youth Pledge">promoted by nationalists in the 1920s</a> and achieved official status under the name <i>Bahasa Indonesia</i> in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> As a result of centuries-long contact with other languages, it is rich in local and foreign influences, including from Javanese, Sundanese, Minangkabau, Hindi, Sanskrit, Chinese, Arabic, Dutch, Portuguese and English.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup> Nearly every Indonesian speaks the language due to its widespread use in education, academics, communications, business, politics, and mass media. Most Indonesians also speak at least one of more than 700 local languages,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup> often as their first language. Most belong to the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian language family</a>, while there are over 270 <a href="/wiki/Papuan_languages" title="Papuan languages">Papuan languages</a> spoken in eastern Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup> Of these, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> is the most widely spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1930, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and other Europeans (<i><a href="/wiki/Totok" title="Totok">Totok</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Eurasians</a>, and derivative people like the <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indos</a>, numbered 240,000 or 0.4% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup> Historically, they constituted only a tiny fraction of the native population and remain so today. Also, the Dutch language never had a substantial number of speakers or official status despite the Dutch presence for almost 350 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaker1998202_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaker1998202-226">[224]</a></sup> The small minorities that can speak it or <a href="/wiki/Dutch-based_creole_languages" title="Dutch-based creole languages">Dutch-based creole languages</a> fluently are the aforementioned ethnic groups and descendants of Dutch colonisers. This reflected the primary purpose of the Dutch colonial empire, which was commercial exchange as opposed to sovereignty over homogeneous landmasses.<sup id="cite_ref-Ward_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward-227">[225]</a></sup> Today, there is some degree of fluency by either educated members of the oldest generation or legal professionals,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmmon20052017_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmmon20052017-228">[226]</a></sup> as specific law codes are still only available in Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBooij19992_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBooij19992-229">[227]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Religion in Indonesia">Religion in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>While the constitution stipulates religious freedom,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UUD45_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UUD45-118">[117]</a></sup> the government officially recognises only <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Religion in Indonesia">six religions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Indonesia" title="Protestantism in Indonesia">Protestantism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Indonesia">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Indonesia" title="Buddhism in Indonesia">Buddhism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_for_the_Confucian_Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Supreme Council for the Confucian Religion in Indonesia">Confucianism</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marshall_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-232">[230]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous religions">indigenous religions</a> only partly acknowledged.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshall_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-232">[230]</a></sup> Indonesia is the world's most populous Muslim-majority country<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs2001379_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs2001379-233">[231]</a></sup> with 227&nbsp;million adherents in 2017, with the majority being <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunnis</a> (99%).<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Shia Islam in Indonesia">Shias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_in_Indonesia" title="Ahmadiyya in Indonesia">Ahmadis</a> respectively constitute 1% (1–3&nbsp;million) and 0.2% (200,000–400,000) of the Muslim population.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshall_232-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-232">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> Almost 11% of Indonesians are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, while the rest are Hindus, Buddhists, and others. Most <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> are <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup> and most <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> are <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesians" title="Chinese Indonesians">Chinese Indonesians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta,_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/220px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/330px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/440px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1575" data-file-height="1180"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta,_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> shrine dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Sri_Baduga_Maharaja" title="Sri Baduga Maharaja">Sri Baduga Maharaja</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkarta" title="Pura Parahyangan Agung Jagatkarta">Pura Parahyangan Agung Jagatkarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogor" title="Bogor">Bogor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> has left a lasting impact in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Indonesia" title="Culture of Indonesia">Indonesian art and culture</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The natives of the Indonesian archipelago originally practised indigenous <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dynamism_(metaphysics)" title="Dynamism (metaphysics)">dynamism</a>, beliefs that are common to <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ooi_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi-238">[236]</a></sup> They worshipped and revered ancestral spirit, and believed that supernatural spirits (<i><a href="/wiki/Hyang" title="Hyang">hyang</a></i>) might inhabit certain places such as large trees, stones, forests, mountains, or sacred sites.<sup id="cite_ref-Ooi_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi-238">[236]</a></sup> Examples of Indonesian native belief systems include the <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Wiwitan" title="Sunda Wiwitan">Sunda Wiwitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kaharingan" title="Kaharingan">Kaharingan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Kejaw%C3%A8n" title="Kejawèn">Kejawèn</a>. They have had a significant impact on how other faiths are practised, evidenced by a large proportion of people—such as the Javanese <a href="/wiki/Abangan" title="Abangan">abangan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balinese_Hinduism" title="Balinese Hinduism">Balinese Hindus</a>, and Dayak Christians—practising a less <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> form of their religion.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hindu</a> influences reached the archipelago as early as the first century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdoms_of_Sunda" title="Kingdoms of Sunda">Kingdom</a> of <a href="/wiki/Salakanagara" title="Salakanagara">Salakanagara</a> in western Java around 130 was the first historically recorded <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Indianised</a> kingdom in the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Indonesia" title="Buddhism in Indonesia">Buddhism</a> arrived around the 6th century,<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup> and its history in Indonesia is closely related to that of Hinduism, as some empires based on Buddhism had its roots around the same period. The archipelago has witnessed the rise and fall of powerful and influential Hindu and Buddhist empires such as <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shailendra_dynasty" title="Shailendra dynasty">Sailendra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a>, and Mataram. Though no longer a majority, Hinduism and Buddhism remain to have a substantial influence on Indonesian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG/220px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG/330px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG/440px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="1276"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a> mass prayer in <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Islam</a> was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> traders of the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> <a href="/wiki/Fiqh" title="Fiqh">fiqh</a>, as well as Sufi traders from the Indian subcontinent and southern Arabian peninsula as early as the 8th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[244]</a></sup> For the most part, Islam overlaid and mixed with existing cultural and religious influences that resulted in a distinct form of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112–14_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112–14-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup> Trade, missionary works such as by the Wali Sanga and Chinese explorer Zheng He, and military campaigns by several sultanates helped accelerate the spread of the religion.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[247]</a></sup> By the end of the 16th century, Islam had supplanted Hinduism and Buddhism as the dominant religion of Java and Sumatra. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/220px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/330px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/440px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> at the <a href="/wiki/St._Mary_of_the_Assumption_Cathedral,_Jakarta" title="St. Mary of the Assumption Cathedral, Jakarta">Jakarta Cathedral</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Indonesia" title="Catholic Church in Indonesia">Catholicism</a> was brought by Portuguese traders and missionaries such as <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a>, who visited and baptised several thousand locals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199125,_26,_28_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199125,_26,_28-250">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[249]</a></sup> Its spread faced difficulty due to the VOC policy of banning the religion and the Dutch hostility due to the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> against Catholic Spain's rule. <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Indonesia" title="Protestantism in Indonesia">Protestantism</a> is mostly a result of <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> missionary efforts during the Dutch colonial era.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199128,_62_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199128,_62-252">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers200522_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers200522-253">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup> Although they are the most common branch, there is a multitude of other denominations elsewhere in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There was a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Indonesia" title="History of the Jews in Indonesia">sizable Jewish presence in the archipelago</a> until 1945, mostly Dutch and some Baghdadi Jews. Since most have left after Indonesia proclaimed independence, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> was never accorded official status, and only a tiny number of Jews remain today, mostly in Jakarta and Surabaya.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup> At the national and local level, Indonesia's political leadership and civil society groups have played a crucial role in interfaith relations, both positively and negatively. The invocation of the first principle of Indonesia's philosophical foundation, Pancasila (the belief in the one and only God) often serves as a reminder of religious tolerance,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[255]</a></sup> though instances of intolerance have occurred. An overwhelming majority of Indonesians consider religion to be essential,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup> and its role is present in almost all aspects of society, including politics, education, marriage, and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Indonesia" title="Public holidays in Indonesia">public holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_health">Education and health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Indonesia" title="Education in Indonesia">Education in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Indonesia" title="Health in Indonesia">Health in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ITB_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/220px-ITB_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/330px-ITB_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/440px-ITB_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="633"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ITB_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bandung Institute of Technology in <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education is compulsory for 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup> Parents can choose between state-run, non-sectarian schools or private or semi-private religious (usually Islamic) schools, supervised by the ministries of Education and Religion, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup> Private international schools that do not follow the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Indonesia#2013_Curriculum" title="Education in Indonesia">national curriculum</a> are also available. The enrolment rate is 93% for primary education, 79% for secondary education, and 36% for tertiary education (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-UIS_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UIS-263">[261]</a></sup> The literacy rate is 96% (2018), and the government spends about 3.6% of GDP (2015) on education.<sup id="cite_ref-UIS_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UIS-263">[261]</a></sup> In 2018, there were more than 4,500 higher educational institutions in Indonesia,<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[262]</a></sup> with the top universities (the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Indonesia" title="University of Indonesia">University of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Institute_of_Technology" title="Bandung Institute of Technology">Bandung Institute of Technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gadjah_Mada_University" title="Gadjah Mada University">Gadjah Mada University</a>) and most others located in Java.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Government expenditure on healthcare is about 3.3% of GDP in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[264]</a></sup> As part of an attempt to achieve universal health care, the government launched the National Health Insurance (<i>Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional</i>, JKN) in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup> It includes coverage for a range of services from the public and also private firms that have opted to join the scheme. In recent decades, there have been remarkable improvements such as rising life expectancy (from 62.3 years in 1990 to 71.7 years in 2019)<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup> and declining child mortality (from 84 deaths per 1,000 births in 1990 to 25.4 deaths in 2017).<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Indonesia continues to face challenges that include maternal and child health, low air quality, malnutrition, high rate of smoking, and infectious diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Indonesia" title="Human rights in Indonesia">Human rights in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg/220px-Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg/330px-Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg/440px-Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="638" data-file-height="439"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Organisasi_Papua_Merdeka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Papuan separatist rally with a flying of the banned <a href="/wiki/Morning_Star_flag" title="Morning Star flag">Morning Star flag</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nearly 80% of Indonesia's population lives in the western parts of the archipelago,<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup> but they are growing at a slower pace than the rest of the country. This situation creates a gap in wealth, unemployment rate, and health between densely populated islands and economic centres (such as <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>) and sparsely populated, disadvantaged areas (such as <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Papua</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[271]</a></sup> Numerous cases of racism and discrimination, especially <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_Chinese_Indonesians" title="Discrimination against Chinese Indonesians">against Chinese Indonesians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people_of_New_Guinea" title="Indigenous people of New Guinea">Papuans</a>, have been well documented; the latter has to do with an <a href="/wiki/Free_Papua_Movement" title="Free Papua Movement">ongoing, decades-long separatist movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[272]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Indonesia" title="LGBT rights in Indonesia">LGBT issues in Indonesia</a> has been relatively obscure. However, in the 2010s (especially after 2016), a wave of anti-LGBT rhetoric has surged rapidly, putting LGBT Indonesians into a frequent subject of intimidation, discrimination, and even violence.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[273]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[274]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Indonesia" title="Culture of Indonesia">Culture of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Indonesia" title="Public holidays in Indonesia">Public holidays in Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The cultural history of the Indonesian archipelago spans more than two millennia. Influences from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-JForshee_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JForshee-277">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a> have historically shaped the cultural, linguistic and religious makeup of the archipelago. As a result, modern-day Indonesia has a multicultural, multilingual and multi-ethnic society,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BPS_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> with a complex cultural mixture that differs significantly from the original indigenous cultures. Indonesia currently holds <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">eleven items of UNESCO's Intangible Cultural Heritage</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">wayang</a> puppet theatre, <a href="/wiki/Kris" title="Kris">kris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pencak_silat" title="Pencak silat">pencak silat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">angklung</a>, and the three genres of traditional <a href="/wiki/Balinese_dance" title="Balinese dance">Balinese dance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_art" title="Indonesian art">Indonesian art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Indonesia" title="Architecture of Indonesia">Architecture of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/220px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/330px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/440px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="726"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Balinese painting depicting <a href="/wiki/Cockfighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Cockfighting">cockfighting</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesian arts include both age-old art forms developed through centuries and a recently developed <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>. Despite often displaying local ingenuity, Indonesian arts have absorbed foreign influences—most notably from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, as a result of contacts and interactions facilitated, and often motivated, by trade.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[279]</a></sup> Painting is an <a href="/wiki/Balinese_art" title="Balinese art">established and developed art in Bali</a>, where its people are famed for their artistry. Their painting tradition started as classical <a href="/wiki/Kamasan" title="Kamasan">Kamasan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a> style visual narrative, derived from visual art discovered on <i><a href="/wiki/Candi_of_Indonesia" title="Candi of Indonesia">candi</a></i> bas reliefs in eastern Java.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/220px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/330px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/440px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An avenue of <a href="/wiki/Tongkonan" title="Tongkonan">Tongkonan</a> houses in a <a href="/wiki/Toraja" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraja">Torajan</a> village, <a href="/wiki/South_Sulawesi" title="South Sulawesi">South Sulawesi</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There have been numerous discoveries of <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_art" title="Megalithic art">megalithic sculptures</a> in Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[281]</a></sup> Subsequently, tribal art has flourished within the culture of <a href="/wiki/Nias_people" title="Nias people">Nias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Batak people">Batak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asmat_people" title="Asmat people">Asmat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toraja" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraja">Toraja</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup> Wood and stone are common materials used as the media for sculpting among these tribes. Between the 8th and 15th centuries, the Javanese civilisation has developed a refined stone sculpting art and architecture which was influenced by Hindu-Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">Dharmic</a> civilisation. The temples of <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prambanan" title="Prambanan">Prambanan</a> are among the most famous examples of the practice.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As with the arts, Indonesian architecture has absorbed foreign influences that have brought cultural changes and profound effect on building styles and techniques. The most dominant has traditionally been <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_India" title="Architecture of India">Indian</a>; however, Chinese, Arab, and European influences have also been significant. Traditional carpentry, masonry, stone and woodwork techniques and decorations have thrived in vernacular architecture, with numbers of traditional houses' (<i><a href="/wiki/Rumah_adat" title="Rumah adat">rumah adat</a></i>) styles that have been developed. The traditional houses and settlements in the country vary by ethnic groups, and each has a specific custom and history.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[285]</a></sup> Examples include <a href="/wiki/Toraja" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraja">Toraja</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tongkonan" title="Tongkonan">Tongkonan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rumah_Gadang" title="Rumah Gadang">Rumah Gadang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangkiang" title="Rangkiang">Rangkiang</a>, Javanese style <a href="/wiki/Pendopo" class="mw-redirect" title="Pendopo">Pendopo</a> pavilion with <a href="/wiki/Joglo" title="Joglo">Joglo</a> style roof, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Longhouse" title="Longhouse">longhouses</a>, various <a href="/wiki/Rumah_Melayu" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumah Melayu">Malay houses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balinese_architecture" title="Balinese architecture">Balinese houses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balinese_temple" title="Balinese temple">temples</a>, and also different forms of <a href="/wiki/Rice_barn" title="Rice barn">rice barns</a> (<i>lumbung</i>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Music.2C_dance_and_clothing"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Music,_dance_and_clothing">Music, dance and clothing</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Indonesia" title="Music of Indonesia">Music of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Indonesia" title="Dance in Indonesia">Dance in Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_costume_of_Indonesia" title="National costume of Indonesia">National costume of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:169px;max-width:169px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Gamelan_Player_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/167px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="167" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/251px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/334px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="864"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:119px;max-width:119px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Angklung-arumba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/117px-Angklung-arumba.jpg" decoding="async" width="117" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/176px-Angklung-arumba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/234px-Angklung-arumba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="905" data-file-height="981"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:148px;max-width:148px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:97px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tari_Pendet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tari_Pendet.jpg/146px-Tari_Pendet.jpg" decoding="async" width="146" height="97" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tari_Pendet.jpg/219px-Tari_Pendet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tari_Pendet.jpg/292px-Tari_Pendet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:140px;max-width:140px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:97px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/138px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="138" height="97" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/207px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/276px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1600"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Indonesian music and dance. Clockwise from top: A <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a> player, <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a>, Sundanese <a href="/wiki/Jaipongan" title="Jaipongan">Jaipongan</a> Mojang Priangan dance, Balinese <a href="/wiki/Pendet" class="mw-redirect" title="Pendet">Pendet</a> dance.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The music of Indonesia predates historical records. Various indigenous tribes incorporate chants and songs accompanied by musical instruments in their rituals. <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kacapi_suling" title="Kacapi suling">kacapi suling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gong" title="Gong">gong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talempong" title="Talempong">talempong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kulintang" title="Kulintang">kulintang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sasando" title="Sasando">sasando</a> are examples of traditional Indonesian instruments. The diverse world of Indonesian music genres is the result of the musical creativity of its people, and subsequent cultural encounters with foreign influences. These include <a href="/wiki/Qanb%C5%ABs" title="Qanbūs">gambus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qasida" title="Qasida">qasida</a> from the Middle East,<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[286]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Keroncong" class="mw-redirect" title="Keroncong">keroncong</a> from Portugal,<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[287]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dangdut" title="Dangdut">dangdut</a>—one of the most popular music genres in Indonesia—with notable Hindi influence as well as Malay orchestras.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[288]</a></sup> Today, the Indonesian music industry enjoys both nationwide and regional popularity in Malaysia, Singapore, and Brunei,<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup> due to common culture and intelligible languages between <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/170px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/255px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/340px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An Indonesian <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesian dances have a diverse history, with more than 3,000 original dances. Scholars believe that they had their beginning in rituals and religious worship.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[291]</a></sup> Examples include war dances, a dance of <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctors</a>, and dance to call for rain or any agricultural rituals such as <a href="/wiki/Hudoq" title="Hudoq">Hudoq</a>. Indonesian dances derive its influences from the archipelago's prehistoric and tribal, Hindu-Buddhist, and Islamic periods. Recently, modern dances and urban teen dances have gained popularity due to the influence of Western culture, as well as those of Japan and South Korea to some extent. Various traditional dances, however, including those of Java, Bali and Dayak continue to be a living and dynamic tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[292]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indonesia has various styles of clothing as a result of its long and rich cultural history. The national costume has its origins in the indigenous culture of the country and traditional textile traditions. The Javanese <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">Batik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kebaya" title="Kebaya">Kebaya</a><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[293]</a></sup> are arguably Indonesia's most recognised national costume, though they have <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a> origins as well.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-296">[294]</a></sup> Each province has a representation of traditional attire and dress,<sup id="cite_ref-JForshee_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JForshee-277">[275]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Ulos" title="Ulos">Ulos</a> of <a href="/wiki/Batak" title="Batak">Batak</a> from <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a>; <a href="/wiki/Songket" title="Songket">Songket</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a> from Sumatra; and <a href="/wiki/Ikat" title="Ikat">Ikat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sasak_people" title="Sasak people">Sasak</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a>. People wear national and regional costumes during traditional weddings, formal ceremonies, music performances, government and official occasions,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-296">[294]</a></sup> and they vary from traditional to modern attire. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_cinema">Theatre and cinema</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Indonesia" title="Cinema of Indonesia">Cinema of Indonesia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/220px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/330px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/440px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1261"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pandava" title="Pandava">Pandava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> in an act of the <i>Wayang Wong</i> performance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a>, the Javanese, Sundanese, and Balinese <a href="/wiki/Shadow_puppet" class="mw-redirect" title="Shadow puppet">shadow puppet</a> theatre display several mythological legends such as <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup> Other forms of local drama include the Javanese <a href="/wiki/Ludruk" title="Ludruk">Ludruk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ketoprak" title="Ketoprak">Ketoprak</a>, the Sundanese <a href="/wiki/Sandiwara" title="Sandiwara">Sandiwara</a>, Betawi <a href="/wiki/Lenong" title="Lenong">Lenong</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[297]</a></sup> and various Balinese dance drama. They incorporate humour and jest and often involve audiences in their performances.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[298]</a></sup> Some theatre traditions also include music, dancing and the <a href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" class="mw-redirect" title="Pencak Silat">silat</a> martial art such as <a href="/wiki/Randai" title="Randai">Randai</a> from <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau people</a> of West Sumatra. It is usually performed for traditional ceremonies and festivals,<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-randai_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-randai-302">[300]</a></sup> and based on semi-historical Minangkabau legends and love story.<sup id="cite_ref-randai_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-randai-302">[300]</a></sup> Modern performing art also developed in Indonesia with their distinct style of drama. Notable theatre, dance, and drama troupe such as <i>Teater Koma</i> are famous as it often portrays social and political satire of Indonesian society.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[301]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/170px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/255px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/340px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1592" data-file-height="2040"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Advertisement for <i><a href="/wiki/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng" title="Loetoeng Kasaroeng">Loetoeng Kasaroeng</a></i> (1926), the first fiction film produced in the Dutch East Indies
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first film produced in the archipelago was <i><a href="/wiki/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng" title="Loetoeng Kasaroeng">Loetoeng Kasaroeng</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ctrip_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctrip-304">[302]</a></sup> a silent film by Dutch director L. Heuveldorp. The film industry expanded after independence, with six films made in 1949 rising to 58 in 1955. <a href="/wiki/Usmar_Ismail" title="Usmar Ismail">Usmar Ismail</a>, who made significant imprints in the 1950s and 1960s, is generally considered to be the pioneer of Indonesian films.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[303]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guided_Democracy_in_Indonesia" title="Guided Democracy in Indonesia">latter part of the Sukarno era</a> saw the use of cinema for nationalistic, anti-Western purposes, and foreign films were subsequently banned, while the New Order utilised a censorship code that aimed to maintain social order.<sup id="cite_ref-Krishna_Sen_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krishna_Sen-306">[304]</a></sup> Production of films peaked during the 1980s, although it declined significantly in the next decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctrip_304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctrip-304">[302]</a></sup> Notable films in this period include <i><a href="/wiki/Satan%27s_Slave_(1980_film)" title="Satan's Slave (1980 film)">Pengabdi Setan</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/Nagabonar" title="Nagabonar">Nagabonar</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/Tjoet_Nja%27_Dhien" title="Tjoet Nja' Dhien">Tjoet Nja' Dhien</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Catatan_Si_Boy" title="Catatan Si Boy">Catatan Si Boy</a></i> (1989), and <a href="/wiki/Warkop" title="Warkop">Warkop</a>'s comedy films. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">Independent filmmaking</a> was a rebirth of the film industry since 1998, where films started addressing previously banned topics, such as religion, race, and love.<sup id="cite_ref-Krishna_Sen_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krishna_Sen-306">[304]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2005, the number of films released each year steadily increased.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[305]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Riri_Riza" title="Riri Riza">Riri Riza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mira_Lesmana" title="Mira Lesmana">Mira Lesmana</a> were among the new generation of filmmakers who co-directed <i>Kuldesak</i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Petualangan_Sherina" title="Petualangan Sherina">Petualangan Sherina</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/Ada_Apa_dengan_Cinta%3F" title="Ada Apa dengan Cinta?">Ada Apa dengan Cinta?</a></i> (2002), and <i><a href="/wiki/Laskar_Pelangi" title="Laskar Pelangi">Laskar Pelangi</a></i> (2008). In 2016, <i>Warkop DKI Reborn: Jangkrik Boss Part 1</i> smashed box office records, becoming the most-watched Indonesian film with 6.8&nbsp;million tickets sold.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[306]</a></sup> Indonesia has held annual film festivals and awards, including the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Film_Festival" title="Indonesian Film Festival">Indonesian Film Festival</a> (<i>Festival Film Indonesia</i>) that has been held intermittently since 1955. It hands out the <a href="/wiki/Citra_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Citra Award">Citra Award</a>, the film industry's most prestigious award. From 1973 to 1992, the festival was held annually and then discontinued until its revival in 2004. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_media_and_literature">Mass media and literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mass_media_in_Indonesia" title="Mass media in Indonesia">Mass media in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_literature" title="Indonesian literature">Indonesian literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium,_Jakarta,_MetroTV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/220px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/330px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/440px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2551" data-file-height="1748"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium,_Jakarta,_MetroTV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Metro_TV_(Indonesia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro TV (Indonesia)">Metro TV</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium" title="Gelora Bung Karno Stadium">Gelora Bung Karno Stadium</a>, reporting the <a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship" title="2010 AFF Championship">2010 AFF Championship</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Media_of_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Indonesia">Media</a> freedom increased considerably after the fall of the New Order, during which the Ministry of Information monitored and controlled domestic media and restricted foreign media.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[307]</a></sup> The television market includes several national commercial networks and provincial networks that compete with public <a href="/wiki/TVRI" title="TVRI">TVRI</a>, which held a monopoly on TV broadcasting from 1962 to 1989. By the early 21st century, the improved communications system had brought television signals to every village, and people can choose from up to 11 channels.<sup id="cite_ref-frd2011_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frd2011-310">[308]</a></sup> Private radio stations carry news bulletins while foreign broadcasters supply programmes. The number of printed publications has increased significantly since 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-frd2011_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frd2011-310">[308]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like other developing countries, Indonesia began development of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> in the early 1990s. Its first commercial <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a>, PT. Indo Internet began operation in Jakarta in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[309]</a></sup> The country had 171&nbsp;million Internet users in 2018, with a penetration rate that keeps increasing annually.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[310]</a></sup> Most are between the ages of 15 and 19 and depend primarily on mobile phones for access, outnumbering both laptops and computers.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[311]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/170px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/255px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/340px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1234"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pramoedya_Ananta_Toer" title="Pramoedya Ananta Toer">Pramoedya Ananta Toer</a>, Indonesia's most famous novelist. Many considered him to be Southeast Asia's leading candidate for a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[312]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The oldest evidence of writing in the Indonesian archipelago is a series of <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> inscriptions dated to the 5th century. Many of Indonesia's peoples have firmly rooted <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral traditions</a>, which help to define and preserve their cultural identities.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[313]</a></sup> In written poetry and prose, several traditional forms dominate, mainly <a href="/wiki/Syair" title="Syair">syair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantun" title="Pantun">pantun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurindam" title="Gurindam">gurindam</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hikayat" title="List of Hikayat">hikayat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_historical_texts" title="Javanese historical texts">babad</a>. Examples of these forms include <i><a href="/wiki/Syair_Abdul_Muluk" title="Syair Abdul Muluk">Syair Abdul Muluk</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hikayat_Hang_Tuah" title="Hikayat Hang Tuah">Hikayat Hang Tuah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Malay_Annals" title="Malay Annals">Sulalatus Salatin</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Babad_Tanah_Jawi" title="Babad Tanah Jawi">Babad Tanah Jawi</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[314]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Early modern Indonesian literature originates in Sumatran tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[315]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[316]</a></sup> Literature and poetry flourished during the decades leading up to and after independence. <a href="/wiki/Balai_Pustaka" title="Balai Pustaka">Balai Pustaka</a>, the government bureau for popular literature, was instituted in 1917 to promote the development of indigenous literature. Many scholars consider the 1950s and 1960s to be the Golden Age of Indonesian Literature.<sup id="cite_ref-literary_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-literary-319">[317]</a></sup> The style and characteristics of modern Indonesian literature vary according to the dynamics of the country's political and social landscape,<sup id="cite_ref-literary_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-literary-319">[317]</a></sup> most notably the war of independence in the second half of the 1940s and the anti-communist mass killings in the mid-1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[318]</a></sup> Notable literary figures of the modern era include <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chairil_Anwar" title="Chairil Anwar">Chairil Anwar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Yamin" title="Mohammad Yamin">Mohammad Yamin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merari_Siregar" title="Merari Siregar">Merari Siregar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marah_Roesli" title="Marah Roesli">Marah Roesli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pramoedya_Ananta_Toer" title="Pramoedya Ananta Toer">Pramoedya Ananta Toer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ayu_Utami" title="Ayu Utami">Ayu Utami</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_cuisine" title="Indonesian cuisine">Indonesian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/220px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/330px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/440px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2635" data-file-height="1976"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Nasi_Padang" class="mw-redirect" title="Nasi Padang">Nasi Padang</a></i> with <i><a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gulai" title="Gulai">gulai</a></i> and vegetables
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Indonesian cuisine is one of the most diverse, vibrant, and colourful in the world, full of intense flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[319]</a></sup> Many regional cuisines exist, often based upon indigenous culture and foreign influences such as Chinese, European, Middle Eastern, and Indian precedents.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[320]</a></sup> Rice is the leading <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple food</a> and is served with <a href="/wiki/Side_dish" title="Side dish">side dishes</a> of meat and vegetables. Spices (notably chilli), <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>, fish and chicken are fundamental ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[321]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some popular dishes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">nasi goreng</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gado-gado" title="Gado-gado">gado-gado</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">sate</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Soto_(food)" title="Soto (food)">soto</a></i> are ubiquitous and considered as national dishes. The Ministry of Tourism, however, chose <i><a href="/wiki/Tumpeng" title="Tumpeng">tumpeng</a></i> as the official national dish in 2014, describing it as binding the diversity of various culinary traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[322]</a></sup> Other popular dishes include <i><a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a></i>, one of the many <a href="/wiki/Padang_cuisine" title="Padang cuisine">Padang cuisines</a> along with <i><a href="/wiki/Dendeng" title="Dendeng">dendeng</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gulai" title="Gulai">gulai</a></i>. Another fermented food is <i><a href="/wiki/Oncom" title="Oncom">oncom</a></i>, similar in some ways to <i><a href="/wiki/Tempeh" title="Tempeh">tempeh</a></i> but uses a variety of bases (not only soy), created by different fungi, and is prevalent in <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[323]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Indonesia" title="Sport in Indonesia">Sport in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_martial_arts" title="Indonesian martial arts">Indonesian martial arts</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg/170px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg/255px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg/340px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1176" data-file-height="1626"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pencak_Silat_Betawi_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A demonstration of <i><a href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" class="mw-redirect" title="Pencak Silat">Pencak Silat</a></i>, a form of martial arts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sports are generally male-oriented, and spectators are often associated with illegal gambling.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003103_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003103-326">[324]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">Badminton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> are the most popular sports. Indonesia is among the only five countries that have won the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cup" title="Thomas Cup">Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uber_Cup" title="Uber Cup">Uber Cup</a>, the world team championship of men's and women's badminton. Along with <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a>, it is the sport that contributes the most to <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_at_the_Olympics" title="Indonesia at the Olympics">Indonesia's Olympic medal tally</a>. <a href="/wiki/Liga_1_(Indonesia)" title="Liga 1 (Indonesia)">Liga 1</a> is the country's premier football club league. On the international stage, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_national_football_team" title="Indonesia national football team">Indonesia</a> was the first Asian team to participate at the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938</a> as the Dutch East Indies.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[325]</a></sup> On a regional level, Indonesia won a bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/1958_Asian_Games" title="1958 Asian Games">1958 Asian Games</a> as well as two gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/1987_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="1987 Southeast Asian Games">1987</a> and <a href="/wiki/1991_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="1991 Southeast Asian Games">1991 Southeast Asian Games</a> (SEA Games). Indonesia's first appearance at the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a> was in <a href="/wiki/1996_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1996 AFC Asian Cup">1996</a> and successfully qualified for the next three tournaments, although they never make the knockout phase.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[326]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, which has a long history in Indonesia and was part of the first <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Week_(Indonesia)" title="National Sports Week (Indonesia)">National Games</a> (<i>Pekan Olahraga Nasional</i>, PON) in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[327]</a></sup> Some of the famous Indonesian boxers include <a href="/wiki/Ellyas_Pical" title="Ellyas Pical">Ellyas Pical</a>, three times <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Federation" title="International Boxing Federation">IBF</a> <a href="/wiki/Super_flyweight" title="Super flyweight">Super flyweight</a> champion; <a href="/wiki/Nico_Thomas" title="Nico Thomas">Nico Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Rachman" title="Muhammad Rachman">Muhammad Rachman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_John_(boxer)" title="Chris John (boxer)">Chris John</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[328]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Haryanto" title="Rio Haryanto">Rio Haryanto</a> became the first Indonesian to compete in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[329]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sepak_takraw" title="Sepak takraw">Sepak takraw</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Karapan_sapi" title="Karapan sapi">karapan sapi</a></i> (bull racing) in <a href="/wiki/Madura_Island" title="Madura Island">Madura</a> are some examples of traditional sports in Indonesia. In areas with a history of tribal warfare, mock fighting contests are held, such as <i>caci</i> in <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pasola" title="Pasola">pasola</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Sumba" title="Sumba">Sumba</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" class="mw-redirect" title="Pencak Silat">Pencak Silat</a></i> is an Indonesian martial art and in 1987, became one of the sporting events in the SEA Games, with Indonesia appearing as one of the leading competitors. In Southeast Asia, Indonesia is one of the top sports powerhouses by winning the SEA Games ten times since 1977,<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[330]</a></sup> most recently in <a href="/wiki/2011_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="2011 Southeast Asian Games">2011</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[331]</a></sup> </p>

       <ul>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-efn0-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-efn0_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sometimes the nationalistic name of the <b>Unitary State of Republic of Indonesia</b> (<i>Negara Kesatuan Republik Indonesia</i>, NKRI) is used.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-219"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-219">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Small but significant populations of <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">ethnic Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indians</a>, Europeans and Arabs are concentrated mostly in urban areas.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
